       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       receiver was unable to accurately process the changes in frequency and wavelength of the signal it would be receiving from
       <i>
        Huygens
       </i>
       during its descent to Titan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The problem was rectified by changing the distance and angle of
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       trajectory to
       <i>
        Huygens
       </i>
       during the landing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_events_and_discoveries">
        Selected events and discoveries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Selected events and discoveries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens_timeline" title="Cassini–Huygens timeline">
        Cassini–Huygens timeline
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Venus_and_Earth_fly-bys_and_the_cruise_to_Jupiter">
        Venus and Earth fly-bys and the cruise to Jupiter
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Venus and Earth fly-bys and the cruise to Jupiter">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1025" data-file-width="1084" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Picture of the
         <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
          Moon
         </a>
         during flyby
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       space probe performed two
       <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">
        gravitational-assist flybys
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">
        Venus
       </a>
       on April 26, 1998, and June 24, 1999. These flybys provided the space probe with enough momentum to travel all the way out to the
       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">
        asteroid belt
       </a>
       . At that point, the Sun's gravity pulled the space probe back into the inner Solar System.
      </p>
      <p>
       On August 18, 1999, at 03:28 UTC, the craft made a gravitational-assist flyby of the Earth. One hour and 20 minutes before closest approach,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       made its closest approach to the Earth's Moon at 377,000 kilometers, and it took a series of calibration photos.
      </p>
      <p>
       On January 23, 2000,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       performed a flyby of the
       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">
        asteroid
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/2685_Masursky" title="2685 Masursky">
        2685 Masursky
       </a>
       at around 10:00 UTC. It took photos
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the period five to seven hours before the flyby at a distance of 1.6 million kilometers, and a diameter of 15 to 20 km was estimated for the asteroid.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Jupiter_flyby">
        Jupiter flyby
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Jupiter flyby">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3207" data-file-width="2260" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg/220px-Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg/330px-Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg/440px-Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Jupiter_from_Cassini.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">
          Jupiter
         </a>
         flyby picture
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       made its closest approach to Jupiter on December 30, 2000, and made many scientific measurements. About 26,000 images of Jupiter, its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jupiter%27s_rings" title="Jupiter's rings">
        faint rings
       </a>
       , and its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jupiter%27s_moons" title="Jupiter's moons">
        moons
       </a>
       were taken during the six month flyby. It produced the most detailed global color portrait of the planet yet (see image at right), in which the smallest visible features are approximately 60 km (37 mi) across.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="959" data-file-width="999" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg/220px-PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg/330px-PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg/440px-PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA02879_-_A_New_Year_for_Jupiter_and_Io.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Cassini
         </i>
         photographed Io
         <a href="/wiki/Transit_(astronomy)" title="Transit (astronomy)">
          transiting
         </a>
         Jupiter on January 1, 2001.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A major finding of the flyby, announced on March 6, 2003, was of Jupiter's atmospheric circulation. Dark "belts" alternate with light "zones" in the atmosphere, and scientists had long considered the zones, with their pale clouds, to be areas of upwelling air, partly because many clouds on Earth form where air is rising. But analysis of
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       imagery showed that individual storm cells of upwelling bright-white clouds, too small to see from Earth, pop up almost without exception in the dark belts. According to
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anthony_Del_Genio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anthony Del Genio (page does not exist)">
        Anthony Del Genio
       </a>
       of NASA's
       <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Institute_for_Space_Studies" title="Goddard Institute for Space Studies">
        Goddard Institute for Space Studies
       </a>
       , "the belts must be the areas of net-rising atmospheric motion on Jupiter, [so] the net motion in the zones has to be sinking."
      </p>
      <p>
       Other atmospheric observations included a swirling dark oval of high atmospheric-haze, about the size of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Red_Spot" title="Great Red Spot">
        Great Red Spot
       </a>
       , near Jupiter's north pole. Infrared imagery revealed aspects of circulation near the poles, with bands of globe-encircling winds, with adjacent bands moving in opposite directions.
      </p>
      <p>
       The same announcement also discussed the nature of Jupiter's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planetary_ring" title="Planetary ring">
        rings
       </a>
       . Light scattering by particles in the rings showed the particles were irregularly shaped (rather than spherical) and likely originate as ejecta from
       <a href="/wiki/Micrometeorite" title="Micrometeorite">
        micrometeorite
       </a>
       impacts on Jupiter's moons, probably
       <a href="/wiki/Metis_(moon)" title="Metis (moon)">
        Metis
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Adrastea_(moon)" title="Adrastea (moon)">
        Adrastea
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tests_of_general_relativity">
        Tests of general relativity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tests of general relativity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On October 10, 2003, the mission's science team announced the results of tests of
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">
        Albert Einstein
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_theory_of_relativity" title="General theory of relativity">
        general theory of relativity
       </a>
       , performed by using
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_wave" title="Radio wave">
        radio waves
       </a>
       transmitted from the
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       space probe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The radio scientists measured a
       <a href="/wiki/Frequency" title="Frequency">
        frequency
       </a>
       shift in the radio waves to and from the spacecraft, as those passed close to the Sun. According to the general theory of relativity, a massive object like the Sun causes space-time to curve, causing a beam of radiowaves (or light, or any form of
       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">
        electromagnetic radiation
       </a>
       ) that passes by the Sun to travel farther (known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shapiro_delay" title="Shapiro delay">
        Shapiro time delay
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Although some measurable deviations from the values calculated using the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_theory_of_relativity" title="General theory of relativity">
        general theory of relativity
       </a>
       are predicted by some unusual cosmological models, no such deviations were found by this experiment. Previous tests using radiowaves transmitted by the
       <i>
        Viking
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Voyager
       </i>
       space probes were in agreement with the calculated values from general relativity to within an accuracy of one part in one thousand. The more refined measurements from the
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       space probe experiment improved this accuracy to about one part in 51,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The data firmly support Einstein's general theory of relativity.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_moons_of_Saturn">
        New moons of Saturn
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: New moons of Saturn">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="496" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg/220px-PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg/330px-PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg/440px-PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA18078-PossibleBeginning-NewMoonOfPlanetSaturn-20130415.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The possible formation of a new
         <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">
          moon
         </a>
         was captured on April 15, 2013.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In total, the
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       mission discovered seven new moons orbiting Saturn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Using images taken by
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       , researchers discovered
       <a href="/wiki/Methone_(moon)" title="Methone (moon)">
        Methone
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pallene_(moon)" title="Pallene (moon)">
        Pallene
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Polydeuces_(moon)" title="Polydeuces (moon)">
        Polydeuces
       </a>
       in 2004,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although later analysis revealed that
       <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">
        Voyager 2
       </a>
       had photographed Pallene in its 1981 flyby of the ringed planet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="328" data-file-width="402" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg/220px-Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg/330px-Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moon_Daphnis_S2005_S1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Discovery photograph of moon
         <a href="/wiki/Daphnis_(moon)" title="Daphnis (moon)">
          Daphnis
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On May 1, 2005, a new moon was discovered by
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keeler_gap" title="Keeler gap">
        Keeler gap
       </a>
       . It was given the designation S/2005 S 1 before being named
       <a href="/wiki/Daphnis_(moon)" title="Daphnis (moon)">
        Daphnis
       </a>
       . A fifth new moon was discovered by
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       on May 30, 2007, and was provisionally labeled S/2007 S 4. It is now known as
       <a href="/wiki/Anthe_(moon)" title="Anthe (moon)">
        Anthe
       </a>
       . A press release on February 3, 2009 showed a sixth new moon found by
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       . The moon is approximately 1/3 of a mile (500 m) in diameter within the G-ring of the ring system of Saturn, and is now named
       <a href="/wiki/Aegaeon_(moon)" title="Aegaeon (moon)">
        Aegaeon
       </a>
       (formerly S/2008 S 1).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A press release on November 2, 2009 mentions the seventh new moon found by
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       on July 26, 2009. It is presently labeled
       <a href="/wiki/S/2009_S_1" title="S/2009 S 1">
        S/2009 S 1
       </a>
       and is approximately 300 m (1000 ft) in diameter in the B-ring system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On April 14, 2014, NASA scientists reported the possible beginning of a new moon in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Ring" title="A Ring">
        A Ring
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">
        planet
       </a>
       Saturn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140414a_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140414a-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phoebe_flyby">
        Phoebe flyby
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Phoebe flyby">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3455" data-file-width="5182" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg/300px-Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg/450px-Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg/600px-Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phoebe_arrival_and_departure_mosaics.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Cassini
         </i>
         arrival (left) and departure mosaics of
         <a href="/wiki/Phoebe_(moon)" title="Phoebe (moon)">
          Phoebe
         </a>
         (2004)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On June 11, 2004,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       flew by the moon
       <a href="/wiki/Phoebe_(moon)" title="Phoebe (moon)">
        Phoebe
       </a>
       . This was the first opportunity for close-up studies of this moon (
       <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">
        Voyager 2
       </a>
       performed a distant flyby in 1981 but returned no detailed images). It also was
       <i>
        Cassini's
       </i>
       only possible flyby for Phoebe due to the mechanics of the available orbits around Saturn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first close-up images were received on June 12, 2004, and mission scientists immediately realized that the surface of Phoebe looks different from asteroids visited by spacecraft. Parts of the heavily cratered surface look very bright in those pictures, and it is currently believed that a large amount of water ice exists under its immediate surface.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saturn_rotation">
        Saturn rotation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Saturn rotation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In an announcement on June 28, 2004,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       program scientists described the measurement of the rotational period of Saturn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because there are no fixed features on the surface that can be used to obtain this period, the repetition of radio emissions was used. This new data agreed with the latest values measured from Earth, and constituted a puzzle to the scientists. It turns out that the radio rotational period had changed since it was first measured in 1980 by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">
         Voyager 1
        </a>
       </i>
       , and it was now 6 minutes longer. This, however, does not indicate a change in the overall spin of the planet, but is thought to be due to movement of the source of the radio emissions to a different latitude, at which the rotation rate is different.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orbiting_Saturn">
        Orbiting Saturn
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Orbiting Saturn">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2233" data-file-width="4613" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg/300px-Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg/450px-Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg/600px-Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_during_Equinox.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Saturn reached equinox in 2008, shortly after the end of the prime mission.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On July 1, 2004, the spacecraft flew through the gap between the
       <a href="/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn" title="Rings of Saturn">
        F and G rings
       </a>
       and achieved
       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">
        orbit
       </a>
       , after a seven-year voyage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carolyn_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-carolyn-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was the first spacecraft to ever orbit Saturn.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Saturn Orbital Insertion (SOI) maneuver performed by
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       was complex, requiring the craft to orient its High-Gain Antenna away from Earth and along its flight path, to shield its instruments from particles in Saturn's rings. Once the craft crossed the ring plane, it had to rotate again to point its engine along its flight path, and then the engine fired to decelerate the craft by 622 meters/s to allow Saturn to capture it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       was captured by Saturn's gravity at around 8:54 pm
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Daylight_Time" title="Pacific Daylight Time">
        Pacific Daylight Time
       </a>
       on June 30, 2004. During the maneuver
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       passed within 20,000 km (12,000 mi) of Saturn's cloud tops.
      </p>
      <p>
       When Cassini was in Saturnian orbit, departure from the Saturn system was evaluated in 2008 during end of mission planning.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spilker_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-spilker-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2016)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Titan_flybys">
        Titan flybys
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Titan flybys">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Titan_globe.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2575" data-file-width="2575" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Titan_globe.jpg/220px-Titan_globe.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Titan_globe.jpg/330px-Titan_globe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Titan_globe.jpg/440px-Titan_globe.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Titan_globe.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">
          Titan's
         </a>
         surface was imaged by looking through the atmosphere in 2004, but some clouds remain visible.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       had its first flyby of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturn%27s" title="Saturn's">
        Saturn's
       </a>
       largest moon,
       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">
        Titan
       </a>
       , on July 2, 2004, a day after orbit insertion, when it approached to within 339,000 km (211,000 mi) of Titan. Images taken through special filters (able to see through the moon's global haze) showed south polar clouds thought to be composed of
       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">
        methane
       </a>
       and surface features with widely differing brightness. On October 27, 2004, the spacecraft executed the first of the 45 planned close flybys of Titan when it passed a mere 1,200 kilometers above the moon. Almost four
       <a href="/wiki/Gigabit" title="Gigabit">
        gigabits
       </a>
       of data were collected and transmitted to Earth, including the first radar images of the moon's haze-enshrouded surface. It revealed the surface of Titan (at least the area covered by radar) to be relatively level, with topography reaching no more than about 50 meters in altitude. The flyby provided a remarkable increase in imaging resolution over previous coverage. Images with up to 100 times better resolution were taken and are typical of resolutions planned for subsequent Titan flybys. Cassini collected pictures of Titan and the lakes of methane were similar to the lakes of Earth.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Huygens_lands_on_Titan">
        <i>
         Huygens
        </i>
        lands on Titan
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Huygens lands on Titan">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Huygens_(spacecraft)" title="Huygens (spacecraft)">
        Huygens (spacecraft)
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em">
       <caption>
        External image
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left">
         <img alt="" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/16px-Searchtool.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/24px-Searchtool.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/32px-Searchtool.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>
         <a class="external text" href="http://esamultimedia.esa.int/docs/titanraw/index.htm" rel="nofollow">
          Raw images from the
          <i>
           Huygens
          </i>
          probe descent on 14 January 2005 (37 pages)
         </a>
         <br/>
         © ESA/NASA/JPL/U. of Arizona.
         <small>
          (ESA hosting)
         </small>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       released the
       <i>
        Huygens
       </i>
       probe on December 25, 2004, by means of a spring and spiral rails intended to rotate the probe for greater stability. It entered the atmosphere of Titan on January 14, 2005, and after a two-and-a-half-hour descent landed on solid ground.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170914_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170914-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       successfully relayed 350 of the pictures that it received from
       <i>
        Huygens
       </i>
       of its descent and landing site, a software error failed to turn on one of the
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       receivers and caused the loss of another 350 pictures. While landing, for caution, NASA loaded Huygens with 3 parachutes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Selding_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Selding-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Enceladus_flybys">
        Enceladus flybys
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Enceladus flybys">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2876" data-file-width="3750" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg/220px-Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg/330px-Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg/440px-Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enceladus_PIA06191.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of Enceladus's
         <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">
          Europa
         </a>
         -like surface with the
         <a href="/wiki/Labtayt_Sulci" title="Labtayt Sulci">
          Labtayt Sulci
         </a>
         fractures at center and the Ebony (left) and Cufa dorsa at lower left; imaged by
         <i>
          Cassini
         </i>
         on February 17, 2005
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the first two close flybys of the moon
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enceladus_(moon)" title="Enceladus (moon)">
        Enceladus
       </a>
       in 2005,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       discovered a deflection in the local magnetic field that is characteristic for the existence of a thin but significant atmosphere. Other measurements obtained at that time point to ionized water vapor as its main constituent.
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       also observed water ice geysers erupting from the south pole of Enceladus, which gives more credibility to the idea that Enceladus is supplying the particles of Saturn's E ring. Mission scientists began to suspect that there may be pockets of liquid water near the surface of the moon that fuel the eruptions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On March 12, 2008,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       made a close fly-by of Enceladus, passing within 50 km of the moon's surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The spacecraft passed through the plumes extending from its southern geysers, detecting water, carbon dioxide and various hydrocarbons with its mass spectrometer, while also mapping surface features that are at much higher temperature than their surroundings with the infrared spectrometer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       was unable to collect data with its cosmic dust analyzer due to an unknown software malfunction.
      </p>
      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">
         Wikinews has related news:
         <i>
          <b>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Cassini_discovers_organic_material_on_Saturn_moon" title="wikinews:Cassini discovers organic material on Saturn moon">
            Cassini discovers organic material on Saturn moon
           </a>
          </b>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       On November 21, 2009,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       made its eighth flyby of Enceladus,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       this time with a different geometry, approaching within 1,600 kilometers (990 mi) of the surface. The Composite Infrared Spectrograph (CIRS) instrument produced a map of thermal emissions from the
       <a href="/wiki/Tiger_stripes_(Enceladus)" title="Tiger stripes (Enceladus)">
        Baghdad Sulcus 'tiger stripe'
       </a>
       . The data returned helped create a detailed and high resolution mosaic image of the southern part of the moon's Saturn-facing hemisphere.
      </p>
      <p>
       On April 3, 2014, nearly ten years after
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       entered Saturn's orbit, NASA reported evidence of a large salty internal ocean of liquid water in Enceladus. The presence of an internal salty ocean in contact with the moon's rocky core, places Enceladus "among the most likely places in the Solar System to host
       <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">
        alien microbial life
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140403_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140403-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20140404_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20140404-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian-20140403_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guardian-20140403-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On June 30, 2014, NASA celebrated ten years of
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       exploring Saturn and
       <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Saturn" title="Moons of Saturn">
        its moons
       </a>
       , highlighting the discovery of water activity on Enceladus among other findings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140625_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140625-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In September 2015, NASA announced that gravitational and imaging data from
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       were used to analyze the
       <a href="/wiki/Libration" title="Libration">
        librations
       </a>
       of Enceladus' orbit and determined that the moon's surface is not rigidly joined to its core, concluding that the underground ocean must therefore be global in extent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On October 28, 2015,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       performed a close flyby of Enceladus, coming within 49 km (30 mi) of the surface, and passing through the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Enceladus" title="Atmosphere of Enceladus">
        icy plume above the south pole
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-press-release_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa-press-release-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Radio_occultations_of_Saturn.27s_rings">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_occultations_of_Saturn's_rings">
        Radio occultations of Saturn's rings
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Radio occultations of Saturn's rings">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In May 2005,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       began a series of
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_occultation" title="Radio occultation">
        radio occultation
       </a>
       experiments, to measure the size-distribution of particles in
       <a href="/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn" title="Rings of Saturn">
        Saturn's rings
       </a>
       , and measure the atmosphere of Saturn itself. For over four months, the craft completed orbits designed for this purpose. During these experiments, it flew behind the ring plane of Saturn, as seen from Earth, and transmitted radio waves through the particles. The radio signals received on Earth were analyzed, for frequency, phase, and power shift of the signal to determine the structure of the rings.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1808px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg" title="Upper image: visible color mosaic of Saturn's rings taken on December 12, 2004. Lower image: simulated view constructed from a radio occultation observation on May 3, 2005. Color in the lower image represents ring particle sizes.">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="5776" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg/1800px-Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg/2700px-Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg/3600px-Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg 2x" width="1800"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saturn%27s_rings_in_visible_light_and_radio.jpg" title="File:Saturn's rings in visible light and radio.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         Upper image: visible color mosaic of Saturn's rings taken on December 12, 2004. Lower image: simulated view constructed from a
         <a href="/wiki/Radio_occultation" title="Radio occultation">
          radio occultation
         </a>
         observation on May 3, 2005. Color in the lower image represents ring particle sizes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spokes_in_rings_verified">
        Spokes in rings verified
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Spokes in rings verified">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In images captured September 5, 2005,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       detected spokes in Saturn's rings,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       previously seen only by the visual observer Stephen James O'Meara in 1977 and then confirmed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">
        Voyager
       </a>
       space probes in the early 1980s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
          <span title="A more detailed citation is required. (November 2012)">
           full citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lakes_of_Titan">
        Lakes of Titan
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Lakes of Titan">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Lakes_of_Titan" title="Lakes of Titan">
        Lakes of Titan
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="357" data-file-width="604" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg/220px-PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg/330px-PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg/440px-PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA09184_-Titan_Sea_and_Lake_Superior.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ligeia_Mare" title="Ligeia Mare">
          Ligeia Mare
         </a>
         , on the left, is compared at scale to
         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">
          Lake Superior
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="658" data-file-width="2000" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg/300px-PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg/450px-PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg/600px-PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA18430-SaturnMoon-Titan-EvolvingFeature-20140821.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">
          Titan
         </a>
         - Evolving feature in
         <a href="/wiki/Ligeia_Mare" title="Ligeia Mare">
          Ligeia Mare
         </a>
         (August 21, 2014).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Radar images obtained on July 21, 2006 appear to show lakes of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_hydrocarbon" title="Liquid hydrocarbon">
        liquid hydrocarbon
       </a>
       (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">
        methane
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ethane" title="Ethane">
        ethane
       </a>
       ) in Titan's northern latitudes. This is the first discovery of currently existing lakes anywhere besides on Earth. The lakes range in size from one to one-hundred kilometers across.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On March 13, 2007, the
       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">
        Jet Propulsion Laboratory
       </a>
       announced that it had found strong evidence of seas of methane and ethane in the northern hemisphere of Titan. At least one of these is larger than any of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">
        Great Lakes
       </a>
       in North America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saturn_hurricane">
        Saturn hurricane
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Saturn hurricane">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In November 2006, scientists discovered a storm at the south pole of Saturn with a distinct
       <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">
        eyewall
       </a>
       . This is characteristic of a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">
        hurricane
       </a>
       on Earth and had never been seen on another planet before. Unlike a
       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
        terrestrial
       </a>
       hurricane, the storm appears to be stationary at the pole. The storm is 8,000 kilometers (5,000 mi) across, and 70 kilometers (43 mi) high, with winds blowing at 560 kilometers per hour (350 mph).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Iapetus_flyby">
        Iapetus flyby
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Iapetus flyby">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="579" data-file-width="1024" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg/220px-Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg/330px-Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg/440px-Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iapetus_equatorial_ridge.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Taken on September 10, 2007 at a distance of 62,331 km (38,731 mi) Iapetus's equatorial ridge and surface are revealed. (CL1 and CL2 filters)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1020" data-file-width="1020" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg/220px-Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg/330px-Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg/440px-Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inky_stains_on_a_frozen_moon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Closeup of Iapetus surface, 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On September 10, 2007,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       completed its flyby of the strange, two-toned, walnut-shaped moon,
       <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_(moon)" title="Iapetus (moon)">
        Iapetus
       </a>
       . Images were taken from 1,000 miles (1,600 km) above the surface. As it was sending the images back to Earth, it was hit by a
       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">
        cosmic ray
       </a>
       that forced it to temporarily enter
       <a href="/wiki/Safe_mode_(spacecraft)" title="Safe mode (spacecraft)">
        safe mode
       </a>
       . All of the data from the flyby were recovered.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOX_News_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOX_News-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_extension">
        Mission extension
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Mission extension">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On April 15, 2008,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       received funding for a 27-month extended mission. It consisted of 60 more orbits of
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
        Saturn
       </a>
       , with 21 more close Titan flybys, seven of Enceladus, six of Mimas, eight of Tethys, and one targeted flyby each of
       <a href="/wiki/Dione_(moon)" title="Dione (moon)">
        Dione
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rhea_(moon)" title="Rhea (moon)">
        Rhea
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Helene_(moon)" title="Helene (moon)">
        Helene
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The extended mission began on July 1, 2008, and was renamed the
       <b>
        Cassini Equinox Mission
       </b>
       as the mission coincided with Saturn's
       <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">
        equinox
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_mission_extension">
        Second mission extension
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Second mission extension">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A proposal was submitted to NASA for a second mission extension (September 2010 – May 2017), provisionally named the extended-extended mission or XXM.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This ($60M pa) was approved in February 2010 and renamed the
       <b>
        Cassini Solstice Mission
       </b>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It included
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       orbiting Saturn 155 more times, conducting 54 additional flybys of
       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">
        Titan
       </a>
       and 11 more of Enceladus.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Storm_of_2010_and_aftermath">
        Great Storm of 2010 and aftermath
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Great Storm of 2010 and aftermath">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_Storm.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1015" data-file-width="1015" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Saturn_Storm.jpg/220px-Saturn_Storm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Saturn_Storm.jpg/330px-Saturn_Storm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Saturn_Storm.jpg/440px-Saturn_Storm.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_Storm.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Northern hemisphere storm in 2011
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On October 25, 2012,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       witnessed the aftermath of the massive
       <a href="/wiki/Great_White_Spot" title="Great White Spot">
        Great White Spot
       </a>
       storm that recurs roughly every 30 years on Saturn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Data from the composite infrared spectrometer (CIRS) instrument indicated a powerful discharge from the storm that caused a temperature spike in the stratosphere of Saturn 83 K (83 °C; 149 °F) above normal. Simultaneously, a huge increase in
       <a href="/wiki/Ethylene" title="Ethylene">
        ethylene
       </a>
       gas was detected by NASA researchers at Goddard Research Center in Greenbelt, Maryland. Ethylene is a colorless gas that is highly uncommon on Saturn and is produced both naturally and through man-made sources on Earth. The storm that produced this discharge was first observed by the spacecraft on December 5, 2010 in Saturn's northern hemisphere. The storm is the first of its kind to be observed by a spacecraft in orbit around Saturn as well as the first to be observed at thermal infrared wavelengths, allowing scientists to observe the temperature of Saturn's atmosphere and track phenomena that are invisible to the naked eye. The spike of ethylene gas that was produced by the storm reached levels that were 100 times more than those thought possible for Saturn. Scientists have also determined that the storm witnessed was the largest, hottest stratospheric vortex ever detected in the Solar System, initially being larger than Jupiter's
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Red_Spot" title="Great Red Spot">
        Great Red Spot
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Venus_transit">
        Venus transit
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Venus transit">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On December 21, 2012,
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       observed a
       <a href="/wiki/Transit_of_Venus" title="Transit of Venus">
        transit of Venus
       </a>
       across the Sun.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cas_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cas-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The VIMS instrument analyzed sunlight passing though the Venusian atmosphere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cas_94-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cas-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       VIMS previously observed the transit of exoplanet
       <a href="/wiki/HD_189733_b" title="HD 189733 b">
        HD 189733 b
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cas_94-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cas-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Day_the_Earth_Smiled">
        <i>
         The Day the Earth Smiled
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: The Day the Earth Smiled">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1750" data-file-width="4500" height="86" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg/220px-The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg/330px-The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg/440px-The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Day_the_Earth_smiled.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          The Day the Earth Smiled
         </i>
         -
         <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
          Saturn
         </a>
         with some of its moons,
         <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
          Earth
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">
          Venus
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
          Mars
         </a>
         as visible in this
         <i>
          Cassini
         </i>
         montage (July 19, 2013)
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20131112_95-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20131112-95">
           [95]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/The_Day_the_Earth_Smiled" title="The Day the Earth Smiled">
        The Day the Earth Smiled
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       On July 19, 2013, the probe was pointed towards Earth to capture an image of the Earth and the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       , as part of a natural light, multi-image portrait of the entire Saturn system. The event was unique as it was the first time NASA informed the public that a long-distance photo was being taken in advance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20131112_95-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20131112-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Earth_Shot_2013_96-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Earth_Shot_2013-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The imaging team said they wanted people to smile and wave to the skies, with
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       scientist,
       <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Porco" title="Carolyn Porco">
        Carolyn Porco
       </a>
       , describing the moment as a chance to "celebrate life on the
       <a href="/wiki/Pale_Blue_Dot#Reflections" title="Pale Blue Dot">
        Pale Blue Dot
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rhea_flyby">
        Rhea flyby
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Rhea flyby">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On February 10, 2015, the
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       spacecraft visited
       <a href="/wiki/Rhea_(moon)" title="Rhea (moon)">
        Rhea
       </a>
       more closely, coming within 47,000 km (29,000 mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The spacecraft observed the moon with its cameras producing some of the highest resolution color images yet of Rhea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Return_to_Rhea_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Return_to_Rhea-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperion_flyby">
        Hyperion flyby
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Hyperion flyby">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       performed its latest flyby of Saturn's moon
       <a href="/wiki/Hyperion_(moon)" title="Hyperion (moon)">
        Hyperion
       </a>
       on May 31, 2015, at a distance of about 34,000 km (21,000 mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-next2015_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-next2015-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:388px;max-width:388px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">

          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">

           <br/>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dione_flyby">
        Dione flyby
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Dione flyby">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       performed its last flyby of Saturn's moon
       <a href="/wiki/Dione_(moon)" title="Dione (moon)">
        Dione
       </a>
       on August 17, 2015, at a distance of about 475 km (295 mi). A previous flyby was performed on June 16.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dione2015_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dione2015-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hexagon_changes_color">
        Hexagon changes color
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Hexagon changes color">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn%27s_hexagon" title="Saturn's hexagon">
        Saturn's hexagon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Between 2012 and 2016, the persistent hexagonal cloud pattern at Saturn's north pole changed from a mostly blue color to more of a golden color.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl.nasa.gov_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jpl.nasa.gov-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One theory for this is a seasonal change: extended exposure to sunlight may be creating haze as the pole swivels toward the sun.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl.nasa.gov_102-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-jpl.nasa.gov-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was previously noted that there was less blue color overall on Saturn between 2004 and 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planetary.org_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-planetary.org-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="910" data-file-width="810" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg/190px-PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg/285px-PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg/380px-PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg 2x" width="190"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA21049_Changing_Colors_in_Saturn%27s_North.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <center>
          2012 and 2016:
          <br/>
          hexagon color changes
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1034" data-file-width="2063" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif/450px-PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif/675px-PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif/900px-PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif 2x" width="450"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA21611_-_Saturn%27s_Hexagon_as_Summer_Solstice_Approaches.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <center>
          2013 and 2017:
          <br/>
          hexagon color changes
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Finale_and_destruction">
        Grand Finale and destruction
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Grand Finale and destruction">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Cassini_retirement" title="Cassini retirement">
        Cassini retirement
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        's
       </span>
       end involved a series of close Saturn passes, approaching within the
       <a href="/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn" title="Rings of Saturn">
        rings
       </a>
       , then an entry into Saturn's atmosphere on September 15, 2017, to destroy the spacecraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170914_5-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170914-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170908_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170908-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spilker_70-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-spilker-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This method was chosen because it is imperative to ensure
       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_protection" title="Planetary protection">
        protection
       </a>
       and prevent biological contamination to any of the moons of Saturn thought to offer potential
       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">
        habitability
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2008 a number of options were evaluated to achieve this goal, each with varying funding, scientific, and technical challenges.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cass_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cass-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A short period Saturn impact for an end of mission was rated "excellent" with the reasons "D-ring option satisfies unachieved AO goals; cheap and easily achievable" while collision with an icy moon was rated "good" for being "cheap and achievable anywhere/time".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cass_105-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cass-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On November 29, 2016, the spacecraft performed a Titan flyby that took it to the gateway of F-ring orbits: This was the start of the Grand Finale phase culminating in its impact with the planet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A final Titan flyby on April 22, 2017, changed the orbit again to fly through the gap between Saturn and its inner ring days later on April 26.
       <i>
        Cassini
       </i>
       passed about 3,100 km (1,900 mi) above Saturn's cloud layer and 320 km (200 mi) from the visible edge of the inner ring; it successfully took images of Saturn's atmosphere and began returning data the next day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa20170427_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa20170427-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After a further 22 orbits through the gap, the mission was ended with a dive into Saturn's atmosphere on September 15; signal was lost at 7:55:46 AM
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Daylight_Savings_Time" title="Eastern Daylight Savings Time">
        EDT
       </a>
       on September 15, 2017, just 30 seconds later than predicted. It is estimated that the spacecraft burned up about 45 seconds after the last transmission.
      </p>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:691px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA21896-Saturn-Cassini-ImpactSite-20170915.jpg">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="237" data-file-width="689" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/85/PIA21896-Saturn-Cassini-ImpactSite-20170915.jpg" width="689"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA21896-Saturn-Cassini-ImpactSite-20170915.jpg" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          <center>
           <i>
            Cassini
           </i>
           impact site on
           <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
            Saturn
           </a>
           (
           <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">
            visual
           </a>
           /
           <a href="/wiki/Infrared_spectroscopy" title="Infrared spectroscopy">
            IR
           </a>
           mapping spectrometer; September 15, 2017)
          </center>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
