      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Missions">
        Missions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Missions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The spacecraft operation was organized around a series of missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.equinox.mission_110-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cassini.equinox.mission-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Each is structured according to a certain amount of funding, goals, etc.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.equinox.mission_110-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cassini.equinox.mission-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At least 260 scientists from 17 countries have worked on the
       <i>
        Cassini–Huygens
       </i>
       mission; in addition thousands of people overall worked to design, manufacture, and launch the mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Prime Mission, July 2004 through June 2008.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.tour.prime_112-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-cassini.tour.prime-112">
          [112]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.equinox.start_113-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-cassini.equinox.start-113">
          [113]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Cassini
        </i>
        Equinox Mission was a two-year mission extension which ran from July 2008 through September 2010.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.equinox.mission_110-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-cassini.equinox.mission-110">
          [110]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Cassini
        </i>
        Solstice Mission ran from October 2010 through April 2017.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.equinox.mission_110-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-cassini.equinox.mission-110">
          [110]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.grand.finale_114-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-cassini.grand.finale-114">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
        (Also known as the XXM mission.)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planetary.org_103-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-planetary.org-103">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Grand Finale (spacecraft directed into Saturn), April 2017 to September 15, 2017.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassini.grand.finale_114-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-cassini.grand.finale-114">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:8423_20181_1saturn2016.jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:8423_20181_1saturn2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>

          Saturn by
          <i>
           Cassini
          </i>
          , 2016
         </center>
        </div>

            Epimetheus
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Janus_(moon)" title="Janus (moon)">
            Janus
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Mimas_(moon)" title="Mimas (moon)">
            Mimas
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Pandora_(moon)" title="Pandora (moon)">
            Pandora
           </a>
           and
           <a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(moon)" title="Prometheus (moon)">
            Prometheus
           </a>
           ) (21 November 2017).
          </center>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Glossary">
        Glossary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Glossary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; font-size:90%;">
       <ul>
        <li>
         AACS: Attitude and Articulation Control Subsystem
        </li>
        <li>
         ACS: Attitude Control Subsystem
        </li>
        <li>
         AFC: AACS Flight Computer
        </li>
        <li>
         ARWM: Articulated Reaction Wheel Mechanism
        </li>
        <li>
         ASI: Agenzia Spaziale Italiana, the Italian space agency
        </li>
        <li>
         BIU: Bus Interface Unit
        </li>
        <li>
         CAM: Command Approval Meeting
        </li>
        <li>
         CDS: Command and Data Subsystem—Cassini computer that commands and collects data from the instruments
        </li>
        <li>
         CICLOPS:
         <a class="external text" href="http://ciclops.org/index.php" rel="nofollow">
          Cassini Imaging Central Laboratory for Operations
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         CIMS:
         <i>
          Cassini
         </i>
         Information Management System
        </li>
        <li>
         CIRS: Composite Infrared Spectrometer
        </li>
        <li>
         DCSS: Descent Control Subsystem
        </li>
        <li>
         DSCC: Deep Space Communications Center
        </li>
        <li>
         DSN: Deep Space Network (large antennas around the Earth)
        </li>
        <li>
         DTSTART: Dead Time Start
        </li>
        <li>
         ELS: Electron Spectrometer (part of CAPS instrument)
        </li>
        <li>
         ERT: Earth-received time, UTC of an event
        </li>
        <li>
         ESA: European Space Agency
        </li>
        <li>
         ESOC: European Space Operations Centre
        </li>
        <li>
         FSW: flight software
        </li>
        <li>
         HGA:
         <a href="/wiki/Directional_antenna" title="Directional antenna">
          High Gain Antenna
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         HMCS:
         <i>
          Huygens
         </i>
         Monitoring and Control System
        </li>
        <li>
         HPOC:
         <i>
          Huygens
         </i>
         Probe Operations Center
        </li>
        <li>
         IBS: Ion Beam Spectrometer (part of CAPS instrument)
        </li>
        <li>
         IEB: Instrument Expanded Blocks (instrument command sequences)
        </li>
        <li>
         IMS: Ion Mass Spectrometer (part of CAPS instrument)
        </li>
        <li>
         ITL: Integrated Test Laboratory—spacecraft simulator
        </li>
        <li>
         IVP: Inertial Vector Propagator
        </li>
        <li>
         LGA:
         <a href="/wiki/Directional_antenna" title="Directional antenna">
          Low Gain Antenna
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         NAC: Narrow Angle Camera
        </li>
        <li>
         NASA: National Aeronautics and Space Administration, the United States of America space agency
        </li>
        <li>
         OTM: Orbit Trim Maneuver
        </li>
        <li>
         PDRS: Probe Data Relay Subsystem
        </li>
        <li>
         PHSS: Probe Harness SubSystem
        </li>
        <li>
         POSW: Probe On-Board Software
        </li>
        <li>
         PPS: Power and Pyrotechnic Subsystem
        </li>
        <li>
         PRA: Probe Relay Antenna
        </li>
        <li>
         PSA: Probe Support Avionics
        </li>
        <li>
         PSIV: Preliminary Sequence Integration and Validation
        </li>
        <li>
         PSE: probe support equipment
        </li>
        <li>
         RCS: Reaction Control System
        </li>
        <li>
         RFS: Radio Frequency Subsystem
        </li>
        <li>
         RPX: ring plane crossing
        </li>
        <li>
         RWA: Reaction Wheel Assembly
        </li>
        <li>
         SCET: Spacecraft Event Time
        </li>
        <li>
         SCR: sequence change requests
        </li>
        <li>
         SKR: Saturn Kilometric Radiation
        </li>
        <li>
         SOI: Saturn Orbit Insertion (July 1, 2004)
        </li>
        <li>
         SOP: Science Operations Plan
        </li>
        <li>
         SSPS: Solid State Power Switch
        </li>
        <li>
         SSR: Solid State Recorder
        </li>
        <li>
         SSUP: Science and Sequence Update Process
        </li>
        <li>
         TLA: Thermal Louver Assemblies
        </li>
        <li>
         USO: UltraStable Oscillator
        </li>
        <li>
         VRHU: Variable Radioisotope Heater Units
        </li>
        <li>
         WAC: Wide Angle Camera
        </li>
        <li>
         XXM: Extended-Extended Mission
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>

           <span style="display:none;">

        <li id="cite_note-59">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-59">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          This is currently the best measurement of
          <a href="/wiki/Parameterized_post-Newtonian_formalism" title="Parameterized post-Newtonian formalism">
           post-Newtonian parameter
          </a>
          <i>
           γ
          </i>
          ; the result
          <i>
           γ
          </i>
          = 1 + (2.1 ± 2.3) × 10
          <sup>
           −5
          </sup>
          agrees with the prediction of standard General Relativity,
          <i>
           γ
          </i>
          = 1
         </span>
        </li>

          The Cassini-Huygens Visit to Saturn: A Historic Mission to the Ringed Planet
         </i>
         . Cham: Springer International Publishing Switzerland.
         <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
          ISBN
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-319-07608-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-3-319-07608-9">
          978-3-319-07608-9
         </a>
         .
        </cite>
        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Cassini-Huygens+Visit+to+Saturn%3A+A+Historic+Mission+to+the+Ringed+Planet&amp;rft.place=Cham&amp;rft.pub=Springer+International+Publishing+Switzerland&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft.isbn=978-3-319-07608-9&amp;rft.aulast=Meltzer&amp;rft.aufirst=Michael&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACassini%E2%80%93Huygens">
         <span style="display:none;">
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <cite class="citation news">
         Irene Klotz (Aug 31, 2017).
         <a class="external text" href="http://aviationweek.com/space/cassini-s-ringside-seat-saturn-coming-end" rel="nofollow">
          "Cassini's Ringside Seat At Saturn Coming To An End"
         </a>
         .
         <i>
          Aviation Week &amp; Space Technology
         </i>
         . An epic journey of discovery at Saturn ends, leaving mysteries for future explorers.
        </cite>
        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Aviation+Week+%26+Space+Technology&amp;rft.atitle=Cassini%27s+Ringside+Seat+At+Saturn+Coming+To+An+End&amp;rft.pages=An+epic+journey+of+discovery+at+Saturn+ends%2C+leaving+mysteries+for+future+explorers&amp;rft.date=2017-08-31&amp;rft.au=Irene+Klotz&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Faviationweek.com%2Fspace%2Fcassini-s-ringside-seat-saturn-coming-end&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACassini%E2%80%93Huygens">
         <span style="display:none;">

        </span>
       </li>

         <td class="navbox-abovebelow hlist" colspan="2">
          <div>
           <div class="plainlist">
            <ul>
             <li>
              <span class="nowrap">
               <sup>
                <small>
                 1
                </small>
               </sup>
               A rudimentary prototype of
               <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_internal_combustion_engine" title="History of the internal combustion engine">
                internal combustion piston engine
               </a>
               .
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span class="nowrap">
               <sup>
                <small>
                 2
                </small>
               </sup>
               An early practical type of
               <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Image_projector" title="Image projector">
                image projector
               </a>
               and a precursor to both the modern
               <a href="/wiki/Slide_projector" title="Slide projector">
                slide projector
               </a>
               and the
               <a href="/wiki/Movie_projector" title="Movie projector">
                movie projector
               </a>
               .
              </span>
             </li>
